## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship in materials, where stress depends on strain through constitutive laws (elastic, plastic, or nonlinear) and temperature through thermal softening effects on material properties like elastic modulus and flow stress.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear elasticity with thermal modulus: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - c2 * T) (temperature-dependent Young's modulus, linear in both strain and temperature)
- Hooke's law with thermal strain: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * T) (elastic stress accounting for thermal expansion)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear stress-strain for plastic deformation)
- Power-law with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - c3 * T) (plastic hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook type model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T**c4) (combined strain hardening and thermal softening)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic with power-law hardening)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (strain hardening with Arrhenius-type thermal dependence)
- Voce hardening with temperature: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon)) * (c3 - c4 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal softening)
- Hollomon with thermal factor: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (power-law in both strain and temperature)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Thermal softening ratio: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * (c2 - T)) (exponential thermal dependence of modulus)
- Bilinear model: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 - c1 * T + c2 * T**2) (quadratic temperature dependence of stiffness)
- Arrhenius-type flow stress: sigma = c0 * sinh(c1 * epsilon) * exp(c2 * T) (hyperbolic sine creep law)
- Combined model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (general hardening with exponential thermal factor)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear thermal softening → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or (c0 - c1*T) representing decrease in material strength with temperature
- Strain hardening saturation → Voce-type (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) indicating dislocation density saturation at large strains
- Power-law strain hardening → epsilon**c with 0 < c < 1 (typically c ≈ 0.1-0.5) representing work hardening in metals
- Arrhenius thermal activation → exp(c/T) or exp(-c*T) representing thermally activated deformation mechanisms like dislocation climb or diffusion
- Elastic-plastic transition → Sum of linear term (c0*epsilon) and nonlinear term (c1*epsilon**c2) representing distinct deformation regimes
- Multiplicative decomposition → Stress as product of strain-dependent and temperature-dependent functions f(epsilon)*g(T), reflecting separable constitutive behavior
- Hyperbolic sine flow → sinh(c*epsilon) appearing in high-temperature creep models bridging power-law and exponential regimes
- Polynomial temperature dependence of elastic modulus → E(T) = c0 + c1*T + c2*T**2 reflecting gradual stiffness degradation

- Second term: `5.2295*epsilon^0.9585*(T - 330.2)` = `5.2295*T*epsilon^0.9585 - 1726.1*epsilon^0.9585`

So GT = `5.2295*T*epsilon^0.9585 - 1.1994*T*epsilon - 1726.1*epsilon^0.9585 + 419.83*epsilon`

This has four terms:
1. `T*epsilon^c1` (with c1 ≈ 0.9585)
2. `T*epsilon`
3. `epsilon^c1` (same exponent)
4. `epsilon`

Now I need to find candidates that can express: `a*T*epsilon^p + b*T*epsilon + c*epsilon^p + d*epsilon`

Let me check candidate **7**: `T*c0*epsilon**c1 + T*c2 + c3*epsilon**c1 + c4/(c5*epsilon + c6) + c7*epsilon + c8`

This has `T*c0*epsilon^c1 + T*c2 + c3*epsilon^c1 + c4/(c5*epsilon+c6) + c7*epsilon + c8`. Setting c4=0 and c8=0 gives: `T*c0*epsilon^c1 + T*c2 + c3*epsilon^c1 + c7*epsilon`. But `T*c2` is a term proportional to T only (no epsilon), which GT doesn't have. So c2 must be 0, but then we lose `T*epsilon`. We need `T*epsilon` which isn't `T*c2`.

Wait - GT has `T*epsilon` not `T*constant`. Let me recheck candidates.

Candidate **42**: `T*c0*epsilon**c1 + T*c2/(c3*epsilon + c4) + c5*epsilon**c1 + c6/(c3*epsilon + c4) + c7*epsilon + c8`

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT expression is:
```
c0*epsilon*(-c1*(T - c2) + c3) + epsilon**c4*c5*(T - c6)
```

With c2 = c6 = 330.2004199209183, let me denote this common value as K.

Expanding:
```
c0*epsilon*(-c1*T + c1*K + c3) + c5*epsilon**c4*(T - K)
```
```
= -c0*c1*epsilon*T + c0*(c1*K + c3)*epsilon + c5*T*epsilon**c4 - c5*K*epsilon**c4
```

Let me define new constants:
- A = c5 = 5.2295 (coefficient of T*epsilon^c4)
- B = c4 = 0.9585 (exponent)
- C = -c0*c1 = -23.788 * 0.05042 = -1.1994 (coefficient of T*epsilon)
- D = c0*(c1*K + c3) = 23.788*(0.05042*330.2 + 1) = 23.788*(17.647) = 419.86 (coefficient of epsilon)
- E = -c5*K = -5.2295*330.2 = -1726.8 (coefficient of epsilon^c4)

So GT = A*T*epsilon^B + C*T*epsilon + D*epsilon + E*epsilon^B

GT = T*(A*epsilon^B + C*epsilon) + D*epsilon + E*epsilon^B

The GT has these basis function terms:
1. **T*epsilon^B** (B ≈ 0.9585)
2. **T*epsilon** (linear in both T and epsilon)
3. **epsilon** (linear in epsilon only)
4. **epsilon^B** (fractional power of epsilon only)

Now I need to check which candidates can match this structure. The key question for each candidate is whether it can produce exactly these four terms.

Note that T*epsilon can be absorbed into T*epsilon^B only if B=1, but B≈0.9585≠1. So we need both T*epsilon and T*epsilon^B terms explicitly, OR some mechanism to generate them.

Also note: `T*c2` (which appears in many candidates) represents a term proportional to T alone (no epsilon dependence). The GT has NO such term. So any candidate with `T*c2` must be able to set c2=0 or combine it with other T-only terms to cancel.

Wait, let me re-examine. Looking at the GT more carefully:

GT = A*T*epsilon^B + C*T*epsilon + D*epsilon + E*epsilon^B

There's no pure T term and no constant term. Many candidates have `T*c2` which would need c2=0.

But wait - many candidates also have terms like `c3/(c4*epsilon + c5)`. Can this generate `epsilon` and `epsilon^B` terms? No, `1/(a*epsilon + b)` is a rational function, not a polynomial or fractional power. It cannot equal `D*epsilon + E*epsilon^B`.

So the candidate needs:
1. T*epsilon^B term ✓ (most have T*c0*epsilon**c1)
2. T*epsilon term
3. epsilon term  
4. epsilon^B term

Actually, many candidates have `T*c2` which is just T times a constant - this is NOT T*epsilon. Setting c2=0 eliminates it.

Any term like `c/(c*epsilon + c)` cannot be made equivalent to polynomial/fractional power terms for all epsilon. So candidates relying on rational functions to provide the epsilon and epsilon^B terms will fail.

### Candidate 46: T*c0*epsilon**c1 + T*c2/(c3*epsilon + c4) + c5*epsilon**c1 + c6/(c3*epsilon + c4)

Let me think about this more carefully. We need:
GT = T*A*epsilon^B + T*C*epsilon + D*epsilon + E*epsilon^B

This candidate has:
- T*c0*epsilon^c1 → with c1=B: T*c0*epsilon^B ✓
- T*c2/(c3*epsilon + c4) → rational function of epsilon times T
- c5*epsilon^c1 → c5*epsilon^B ✓
- c6/(c3*epsilon + c4) → rational function of epsilon

We need T*C*epsilon + D*epsilon from the remaining terms: T*c2/(c3*epsilon+c4) + c6/(c3*epsilon+c4).

= (T*c2 + c6)/(c3*epsilon + c4)

This is a rational function. For this to equal T*C*epsilon + D*epsilon = epsilon*(T*C + D), we'd need:

(T*c2 + c6)/(c3*epsilon + c4) = epsilon*(T*C + D)

This means (T*c2 + c6) = epsilon*(T*C + D)*(c3*epsilon + c4) = (T*C + D)*(c3*epsilon^2 + c4*epsilon)

This must hold for all epsilon and T, which is impossible since the left side is independent of epsilon while the right side depends on epsilon.

**Candidate 46 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 47: T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*epsilon/(c2+epsilon) + T*c3*epsilon**c4 + T*c5*epsilon**2 + c6

Set c5=0. Then: T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*epsilon/(c2+epsilon) + T*c3*epsilon^c4 + c6.

With c4=B: T*epsilon + T*epsilon/(c2+epsilon) + T*epsilon^B + const.

T*epsilon/(c2+epsilon) is a rational function that can't be combined with T*epsilon to give just T*epsilon (it adds a nonlinear term). Unless c1=0, then: T*epsilon + T*epsilon^B + const. Missing epsilon and epsilon^B.

**Candidate 47 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 48: T*c0*epsilon**c1 + c2*epsilon**c1 + c3*epsilon/(c4*epsilon + c5) + c6/(c4*epsilon + c5)

= T*c0*epsilon^c1 + c2*epsilon^c1 + (c3*epsilon + c6)/(c4*epsilon + c5)

With c1=B: T*epsilon^B + epsilon^B + (c3*epsilon + c6)/(c4*epsilon + c5).

We need T*epsilon + epsilon from the rational part. But the rational part has no T dependence. So we can't get T*epsilon from it.

**Candidate 48 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 49: Complex rational functions with T. Can't match the required structure.

**Candidate 49 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 50: Similar rational function issues.

**Candidate 50 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

Hmm, none of the candidates seem to match. Let me reconsider whether I'm being too strict.

Let me re-examine the GT more carefully. The GT has four independent basis functions: T*epsilon^B, T*epsilon, epsilon, epsilon^B where B≈0.9585.

None of the candidates have all four of these basis functions available simultaneously without introducing extra irreducible terms. The fundamental issue is that most candidates have only one power c1 for epsilon, and they need two distinct powers (1 and B≈0.9585).

Wait - let me reconsider candidates that have both T*c*epsilon (explicit linear) AND T*epsilon^c1.

Candidates 28, 31, 32, 33, 34, 39 have T*c2*epsilon explicitly.

Let me re-examine **Candidate 34**: T*c0*epsilon**c1 + T*c2*epsilon + T*c3*epsilon**2 + T*c4*epsilon**3 + c5 + c6/(c7*epsilon + c8) + c9*epsilon**c1

Set c3=0, c4=0, c1=B: T*epsilon^B + T*epsilon + c5 + c6/(c7*epsilon+c8) + c9*epsilon^B

= T*epsilon^B + T*epsilon + c9*epsilon^B + c5 + c6/(c7*epsilon+c8)

We need: T*epsilon^B + T*epsilon + D*epsilon + E*epsilon^B

So we need c6/(c7*epsilon+c8) = D*epsilon and c5 = 0 (or absorbed). But c6/(c7*epsilon+c8) ≠ D*epsilon. Unless... no, a rational function 1/(linear) cannot equal a linear function.

What about **Candidate 39**: T*c0*epsilon**c1 + T*c2*epsilon + T*c3*epsilon**2 + T*c4*epsilon**3 + c5*epsilon/(c6*epsilon + c7) + c8/(c6*epsilon + c7) + c9

Set c3=0, c4=0, c1=B: T*epsilon^B + T*c2*epsilon + (c5*epsilon + c8)/(c6*epsilon + c7) + c9

The rational part: (c5*epsilon + c8)/(c6*epsilon + c7). Can this equal D*epsilon + E*epsilon^B? No, because the rational function approaches c5/c6 as epsilon→∞, while D*epsilon + E*epsilon^B → ∞.

None of the candidates can match. Let me double-check by looking for candidates with both explicit epsilon and epsilon^c1 terms (non-T-multiplied) AND both T*epsilon and T*epsilon^c1 terms.

Looking again... **Candidate 33**: T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*log(c2*epsilon+1) + T*c3*epsilon**c4 + T*c5*epsilon**3 + c6*epsilon**c4 + c7

If c1=0, c5=0: T*c0*epsilon + T*c3*epsilon^c4 + c6*epsilon^c4 + c7. With c4=B:
= T*epsilon + T*epsilon^B + epsilon^B + const

Missing epsilon term. Close but not quite.

**Candidate 42**: T*c0*epsilon**c1 + T*c2/(c3*epsilon + c4) + c5*epsilon**c1 + c6/(c3*epsilon + c4) + c7*epsilon + c8

Has T*epsilon^c1, epsilon^c1, epsilon, constant. If c3=0: T*c2/c4 is const*T. Set to 0. Then: T*epsilon^c1 + epsilon^c1 + epsilon + const. With c1=B: T*epsilon^B + epsilon^B + epsilon + const. Missing T*epsilon.

But what if c3≠0? We have T*c2/(c3*epsilon+c4). This is NOT T*epsilon. Can we somehow combine?

Actually, I realize I should look at this problem differently. The GT has a constant term? Let me recheck.

GT = -c0*c1*T*epsilon + c0*(c1*K+c3)*epsilon + c5*T*epsilon^B - c5*K*epsilon^B

= T*(-c0*c1*epsilon + c5*epsilon^B) + c0*(c1*K+c3)*epsilon - c5*K*epsilon^B

No constant term, no pure T term. Four basis functions: T*epsilon, T*epsilon^B, epsilon, epsilon^B.

None of the candidates provide all four without extra irreducible terms. The closest candidates would need both T*epsilon (explicit) and T*epsilon^c1 along with epsilon and epsilon^c1.

Let me check **Candidate 42** once more with c3≠0:

T*c0*epsilon^c1 + T*c2/(c3*epsilon+c4) + c5*epsilon^c1 + c6/(c3*epsilon+c4) + c7*epsilon + c8

With c1=B, this has: T*epsilon^B, T/(c3*epsilon+c4), epsilon^B, 1/(c3*epsilon+c4), epsilon, constant.

For this to match GT, we need T*c2/(c3*epsilon+c4) + c6/(c3*epsilon+c4) + c8 = C*T*epsilon + D*epsilon - (what's already matched).

Actually we already have T*epsilon^B and epsilon^B and epsilon. We need T*epsilon additionally. So:

T*c2/(c3*epsilon+c4) + c6/(c3*epsilon+c4) + c8 should equal C*T*epsilon + (D-c7)*epsilon (adjusting for the epsilon coefficient).

Wait, let me be more careful. GT = A*T*epsilon^B + C*T*epsilon + D*epsilon + E*epsilon^B.

Candidate 42 = c0*T*epsilon^B + T*c2/(c3*epsilon+c4) + c5*epsilon^B + c6/(c3*epsilon+c4) + c7*epsilon + c8

Matching: c0=A, c5=E, c7=D. Then we need:
T*c2/(c3*epsilon+c4) + c6/(c3*epsilon+c4) + c8 = C*T*epsilon

(T*c2 + c6)/(c3*epsilon+c4) + c8 = C*T*epsilon

This requires (T*c2+c6)/(c3*epsilon+c4) = C*T*epsilon - c8

The left side is a decreasing function of epsilon (for c3>0), while the right side is linear in epsilon. These can't be equal for all epsilon.

I'm now quite confident none match. But let me look at a few more carefully.

**Candidate 7 revisited**: T*c0*epsilon**c1 + T*c2 + c3*epsilon**c1 + c4/(c5*epsilon + c6) + c7*epsilon + c8

With c1=B, c2=0, c5=0: T*epsilon^B + epsilon^B + c4/c6 + c7*epsilon + c8 = T*epsilon^B + epsilon^B + epsilon + const.

Missing T*epsilon. No way to get it.

**Candidate 42 revisited with a different approach**: What if we DON'T set c3=0?

We need the rational function part to somehow generate T*epsilon. But T*c2/(c3*epsilon+c4) is a hyperbolic function of epsilon, not linear. It cannot equal C*T*epsilon for all epsilon.

Let me look at candidates with TWO separate epsilon^c powers...

Actually, none of the candidates have two independent fractional power parameters. They all share the same c1 exponent.

The fundamental problem: GT needs T*epsilon (power 1) AND T*epsilon^B (power ≈0.96). Most candidates have only T*epsilon^c1 with one free exponent. Some candidates also have T*c2*epsilon (explicit power 1), which combined with T*epsilon^c1 gives both. But those candidates (28, 31, 32, 34, 39) don't have the non-T epsilon^B term, or have polynomial approximations instead.

Wait, **Candidate 34** has c9*epsilon**c1. With c1=B: T*epsilon^B + T*epsilon + epsilon^B + rational + const. The rational function is the problem - we need D*epsilon from it, but it can't provide that.

Hmm, what if we look at this differently? What if the rational function c6/(c7*epsilon+c8) can be approximated... no, we need EXACT equivalence.

Let me reconsider. Is there any candidate that has: T*epsilon, T*epsilon^c, epsilon, epsilon^c?

Looking through all candidates systematically for these four terms:

- T*epsilon: present in candidates 28, 31, 32, 33, 34, 39, 47, 49 (as T*c*epsilon)
- T*epsilon^c: present in most (as T*c0*epsilon^c1)
- epsilon: present in candidates 1, 4, 7, 8, 10, 11, 18, 22, 23, 28, 31, 32, 33, 34, 37, 39, 42
- epsilon^c: present in candidates 5, 7, 9, 12, 13, 15, 16, 17, 23, 34, 42, 46, 48

Candidates with ALL FOUR: Need T*epsilon AND T*epsilon^c AND epsilon AND epsilon^c.

Candidate 34: T*c0*epsilon^c1 + T*c2*epsilon + T*c3*epsilon^2 + T*c4*epsilon^3 + c5 + c6/(c7*epsilon+c8) + c9*epsilon^c1

Hmm. What if c7=0? Then c6/c8 = const. Still no epsilon.

What about c3*epsilon^2 with c3 set to provide... no, T*c3*epsilon^2 is T times epsilon^2, not epsilon.

**Candidate 33**: T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*log(c2*epsilon+1) + T*c3*epsilon^c4 + T*c5*epsilon^3 + c6*epsilon^c4 + c7

Set c1=0, c5=0: T*epsilon + T*epsilon^B + epsilon^B + const. Missing epsilon.

None of the candidates have all four required basis functions. 

Let me make absolutely sure by checking if any candidate could work through a creative algebraic manipulation I haven't considered.

Actually, wait. Let me reconsider candidates with `c*epsilon/(c*epsilon + c)` type terms. 

`c*epsilon/(c*epsilon + c)` = if we do partial fractions: `1 - c/(c*epsilon + c)` (after normalization). This is bounded and approaches a constant. Can't equal epsilon.

What about combining multiple rational terms? Still rational functions, can't produce power functions.

I'm confident: **No candidate matches the GT.**

GT ≈ (A+C)*T*epsilon + (D+E)*epsilon = T*epsilon*(A+C) + epsilon*(D+E)

But we're told NO approximations allowed. c4 = 0.9585 ≠ 1.

Final answer: No matches.
